    20→### BUG: Inconsistent Error Handling in `sendServiceResult`  
    21→**Severity**: medium  
    22→**Location**: `sendServiceResult`  
    23→**Problem**: The `sendServiceResult` function checks for `result.error` to determine if an error occurred. However, the `result.data` property might also contain an error message or be `null`/`undefined` in case of a service error, which would then be sent with a 200 status code. This can lead to clients receiving successful status codes for operations that actually failed, making error detection difficult. For example, if a service function returns `{ data: null, error: 'Agent not found', status: 404 }`, the current logic correctly sends a 404. export async function pushToGitHub(config: PluginPushConfig): Promise<ServiceResult<PluginPushResult>> {  
  // Validate fork URL  
  if (!config.forkUrl || typeof config.forkUrl !== 'string') {  
    return { error: 'Fork URL is required', status: 400 }  
  }  
  const urlErr = validateGitUrl(config.forkUrl)  
  if (urlErr) return { error: urlErr, status: 400 }  

  // Validate manifest  
  if (!config.manifest || typeof config.manifest !== 'object') {  
    return { error: 'Manifest is required', status: 400 }  
  }  

  // Validate branch  
  const branch = config.branch || 'main'  
  const refErr = validateGitRef(branch)  
  if (refErr) return { error: refErr, status: 400 }  

  // Concurrency guard  
  if (activeOps >= MAX_CONCURRENT_OPS) {  
    return { error: 'Too many concurrent operations. Please wait and try again.', status: 429 }  
  }  

  const pushId = randomUUID().slice(0, 8)  
  const pushDir = path.join(os.tmpdir(), `ai-maestro-push-${pushId}`)  

  try {  
    activeOps++  

    // Clone the fork (use -- to prevent branch from being parsed as a flag)  
    await execPromise('git', ['clone', '--depth', '1', '--branch', branch, '--', config.forkUrl, pushDir], {  
      timeout: 30000,  
    })  

    // Write the manifest  
    await fs.writeFile(  
      path.join(pushDir, 'plugin.manifest.json'),

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #FF9800; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

Now I can see the full picture. The `plugin` field on `PluginSkillSelection` (marketplace variant) is used extensively in:  
1. `services/plugin-builder-service.ts` — validates and uses `skill.plugin` from `PluginSkillSelection`  
2. `components/plugin-builder/SkillPicker.tsx` — constructs `PluginSkillSelection` objects with `plugin: skill.plugin`  
3. `components/plugin-builder/PluginComposer.tsx` — displays `skill.plugin`  

The `skill.plugin` in marketplace components (SkillBrowser, AgentSkillEditor, etc.) refers to the marketplace skill data type, not `PluginSkillSelection` — those are separate. I need to verify what type `SkillPicker` uses.

      if (skill.marketplaceSkillId.includes('..') || path.isAbsolute(skill.marketplaceSkillId) || !SAFE_PATH_SEGMENT_RE.test(skill.marketplaceSkillId)) {
        return `Marketplace skill "${skill.name}": Invalid plugin name "${skill.marketplaceSkillId}"`
      }
```

    20→### BUG: Missing Dependency in `useEffect` for Marketplace Skills  
    21→**Severity**: high  
    22→**Location**: `useEffect` (for loading marketplace skills)  
    23→**Problem**: The `useEffect` hook that loads marketplace skills runs only once on component mount because its dependency array is empty (`[]`). If the `/api/marketplace/skills` endpoint's data changes while the component is mounted (e.g., new skills are installed in the background), the component will not re-fetch and update the `marketplaceSkills` state. This leads to stale data being displayed to the user.  
    24→**Fix**: Add `marketplaceSkills` to the dependency array of the `useEffect` hook. This will cause the effect to re-run whenever `marketplaceSkills` changes, ensuring the component always displays the most up-to-date list of skills. However, this would create an infinite loop. The correct fix is

   273→async function readJsonBody(req: IncomingMessage): Promise<any> {  
   274→  return new Promise((resolve, reject) => {  
   275→    const chunks: Buffer[] = []  
   276→    req.on('data', (chunk: Buffer) => chunks.push(chunk))  
   277→    req.on('end', () => {  
   278→      const body = Buffer.concat(chunks).toString('utf-8')  
   279→      if (!body) return resolve({})  
   280→      try {  
   281→        resolve(JSON.parse(body))  
   282→      } catch (e) {  
   283→        reject(new Error('Invalid JSON body'))  
   284→      }  
   285→    })  
   286→    req.on('error', reject)  
   287→  })  
   288→}  
   289→  
   290→async function readRawBody(req: IncomingMessage): Promise<Buffer> {  
   291→  return new Promise((resolve, reject) => {  
   292→    const chunks: Buffer[] = []  
   293→    req.on('data', (chunk: Buffer) => chunks.push(chunk))  
   294→    req.on('end', () => resolve(Buffer.concat(chunks)))  
   295→    req.on('error', reject)  
   296→  })  
   297→}  
   298→  
   299→function sendJson(res: ServerResponse, statusCode: number, data: any, headers?: Record<string, string>) {  
   300→  let body: string  
   301→  try {  
   302→    body = JSON.stringify(data)  
   303→  } catch (e) {  
   304→    // Circular references or other non-serializable values — send a safe fallback.  
   305→    console.error('[Headless] Failed to serialize response data:', e)  
   306→    body = JSON.stringify({ error: 'Failed to serialize response data' })  
   307→    statusCode = 500  
   308→  }  
   309→  res.writeHead(statusCode, {  
   310→    'Content-Type': 'application/json',  
   311→    'Content-Length': Buffer.byteLength(body),  
   312→    ...headers,  
   313→  })  
   314→  res.end(body)  
   315→}  
   316→  
   317→function sendBinary(res: ServerResponse, statusCode: number, buffer: Buffer | Uint8Array, headers: Record<string, string>) {  
   318→  res.writeHead(statusCode, headers)  
   319→  res.end(buffer)  
   320→}  
   321→  
   322→function sendServiceResult(res: ServerResponse, result: any) {

## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-03-22 20:08:26]*

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #FF9800; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

The findings file is truncated but the pattern for `clearDbGraph` is identical to the other two. Now I have everything I need to apply all four fixes. Let me apply them now.  

**Fix 1: `readJsonBody` — resolve with `{ __readJsonBodyError: true, status: 400, error: '...' }` instead of rejecting.**  

The cleanest approach that doesn't require changing every call site is to have `readJsonBody` resolve with a sentinel and check it once per handler. But the report's recommended fix is to resolve with `{ error, status }` and check it in each handler. However, that would require touching every single call site (dozens of places), which is invasive and error-prone.  

The proper root-cause fix is to make `readJsonBody` resolve with a special error marker, and add a helper that each handler can call once to short-circuit — OR simply have `readJsonBody` send the 400 itself when it can't parse. But that would mix concerns.  

The cleanest single-change fix: wrap the rejection in the `handle` catch, but differentiate a `JsonParseError` class so the top-level handler can return 400 instead of 500.  

</div>


## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-03-22 20:08:32]*

**Old:**  
```
async function readJsonBody(req: IncomingMessage): Promise<any> {
  return new Promise((resolve, reject) => {
    const chunks: Buffer[] = []
    req.on('data', (chunk: Buffer) => chunks.push(chunk))
    req.on('end', () => {
      const body = Buffer.concat(chunks).toString('utf-8')
      if (!body) return resolve({})
      try {
        resolve(JSON.parse(body))
      } catch (e) {
        reject(new Error('Invalid JSON body'))
      }
    })
    req.on('error', reject)
  })
}
```

**New:**  
```
// Sentinel error class so the top-level handler can distinguish a malformed
// request body (client fault → 400) from an internal server fault (→ 500).
class JsonParseError extends Error {
  readonly status = 400
  constructor() {
    super('Invalid JSON body')
    this.name = 'JsonParseError'
  }
}

async function readJsonBody(req: IncomingMessage): Promise<any> {
  return new Promise((resolve, reject) => {
    const chunks: Buffer[] = []
    req.on('data', (chunk: Buffer) => chunks.push(chunk))
    req.on('end', () => {
      const body = Buffer.concat(chunks).toString('utf-8')
      if (!body) return resolve({})
      try {
        resolve(JSON.parse(body))
      } catch (e) {
        // Malformed request body is a client error — reject with a typed error
        // so the top-level catch block can return 400 instead of 500.
        reject(new JsonParseError())
      }
    })
    req.on('error', reject)
  })
}
```

**New:**  
```
      try {
        await matched.handler(req, res, matched.params, query)
      } catch (error) {
        // JsonParseError is a client fault (malformed request body) — return 400,
        // not 500, so callers receive an accurate signal without server-side noise.
        const statusCode = error instanceof JsonParseError ? 400 : 500
        const message = error instanceof JsonParseError ? (error as JsonParseError).message : 'Internal server error'
        if (statusCode === 500) {
          console.error(`[Headless] Error handling ${method} ${pathname}:`, error)
        }
        if (!res.headersSent) {
          sendJson(res, statusCode, { error: message })
        } else if (!res.writableEnded) {
          // Headers already sent (partial response started before the error); just
          // close the connection — we cannot send a new status code at this point.
          res.end()
        }
      }
```

  1368→export function createHeadlessRouter() {

## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-03-22 20:08:02]*

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #FF9800; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

Now I have read the full file. Let me analyze the three findings:  

**Finding 1 (medium):** Adding `setLoadingMarketplace` and `setMarketplaceSkills` to the `useEffect` dependency array. These are React state setter functions, which are guaranteed stable (same reference between renders) by React's contract. The `useEffect` correctly has an empty dependency array `[]` because the fetch URL is static and the effect should run only once on mount. Adding state setters here is not a bug fix — it is a style suggestion. The effect does not depend on any props or external state that would change. SKIPPED: state setter functions are guaranteed stable by React and adding them to the dependency array does not fix any real bug; it is a style/lint preference not a correctness issue.  

**Finding 2 (low):** The `aria-label` uses `skill.description ? skill.description : ...` (ternary with truthiness check) while the visible `<p>` uses `skill.description || ...`. Both behave identically for all falsy values (empty string, null, undefined, 0, false). This is a genuine inconsistency: `? :` with a truthy test and `||` are functionally equivalent here, but making them consistent is correct. This is a real (minor) fix.  

**Finding 3 (low):** `skill.plugin` or `skill.marketplace` could be `null`/`undefined`. I need to check the `MarketplaceSkill` type to determine if these fields can actually be nullish.  

</div>

## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-03-22 20:08:22]*

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #FF9800; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

Now I have everything I need. From the type definition:  

- `MarketplaceSkill.description` is typed as `string` (not optional, not nullable) — line 18  
- `MarketplaceSkill.marketplace` is typed as `string` (not optional, not nullable) — line 21  
- `MarketplaceSkill.plugin` is typed as `string` (not optional, not nullable) — line 23  

So Finding 3 (null/undefined fallbacks for `plugin`/`marketplace`) is not a real bug — the TypeScript type guarantees these fields are always present strings. SKIPPED.  

Finding 2 is a genuine inconsistency: `aria-label` uses the ternary `skill.description ? skill.description : ...` while the visible `<p>` uses `skill.description || ...`. Both are equivalent for non-empty strings but differ conceptually (ternary checks truthiness, `||` is a short-circuit OR). The fix is to make the `aria-label` consistent with the visible text by using `||` as well.  

Now I'll apply the fix.

    23→**Problem**: The `activeOps` counter is decremented in the `catch` block of `buildPlugin` if an error occurs during the initial setup (e.g., `fs.mkdir`, `fs.writeFile`). However, if the `runBuild` function is successfully called (which runs asynchronously), `activeOps` is also decremented in `runBuild`'s `finally` block. This can lead to `activeOps` being decremented twice if an error occurs *after* `runBuild` is initiated but *before* `runBuild`'s `finally` block is reached, or if `runBuild` itself fails. This results in an incorrect count of active operations, potentially allowing more concurrent operations than `MAX_CONCURRENT_OPS` or causing the counter to go negative.  
    24→**Fix**: Remove the `activeOps--` from the `catch` block of `bui  

... [7682 more chars truncated]

## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-03-22 20:01:31]*

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #FF9800; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

I have confirmed the bug. In `buildPlugin`'s `catch` block (line 410), `activeOps--` is called. But `runBuild` already has its own `finally` block (line 642-645) that unconditionally decrements `activeOps`. The problem is: after `activeOps++` at line 344, if `runBuild` is successfully called (fire-and-forget at line 395), the `finally` in `runBuild` will always decrement. But if setup fails before `runBuild` is called (e.g., `fs.mkdir` fails at line 349, `generateManifest` throws, etc.), `runBuild` was never scheduled, so `runBuild`'s `finally` will never run — and `buildPlugin`'s catch block correctly decrements.  

The real issue is: these two paths are mutually exclusive — the `catch` block in `buildPlugin` only fires if an exception propagates before `runBuild` is called, and `runBuild`'s `finally` only fires if `runBuild` was called. So there is NO double-decrement in practice given the current code structure.  

Wait — let me re-examine carefully. Looking at lines 395-406: `runBuild(...)` is called fire-and-forget (no `await`). So the `try` block of `buildPlugin` will not catch errors from `runBuild` itself. The `catch` at line 409 only catches synchronous/awaited errors from lines 349-392. After `runBuild` is called at line 395, the try block returns normally at line 408, so the `catch` at line 409 never fires after `runBuild` is scheduled. The `finally` in `runBuild` handles the decrement.  

BUT — the bug stated in the findings is clear: if an error throws after `activeOps++` (line 344) but before `runBuild` is called at line 395, `buildPlugin`'s catch correctly decrements. If `runBuild` IS called, `buildPlugin`'s catch is not triggered. So there's no double-decrement. However, the comment at line 394 says "activeOps is decremented inside runBuild's finally block" — which means the `catch` block's `activeOps--` at line 410 is the correct handler for the pre-`runBuild` failure path.  

The findings report says: "Remove the `activeOps--` from `buildPlugin`'s catch block." Let me re-examine whether a double-decrement is truly possible. The key question: can both the `catch` at line 409 AND `runBuild`'s `finally` fire for the same operation?  

The answer is YES if something throws between line 395 (when `runBuild` is called) and line 408 (return). Looking at lines 395-408: there's only the `.catch(...)` handler and `return { data: result, status: 202 }`. None of those throw. So actually in the current code, the double-decrement is NOT possible.  

However, the prompt explicitly states the fix: "Remove the duplicate decrement from buildPlugin's catch block (keep only the one in runBuild's finally)." But that would break the case where setup fails BEFORE `runBuild` is called (lines 349-392) — in that scenario, `runBuild` is never called, so its `finally` never runs, and if we remove `activeOps--` from `buildPlugin`'s catch, `activeOps` would never be decremented, leaking the counter permanently.

    19→  
    20→### BUG: Inconsistent Error Handling in `sendServiceResult`  
    21→**Severity**: medium  
    22→**Location**: `sendServiceResult`  
    23→**Problem**: The `sendServiceResult` function checks for `result.error` to determine if an error occurred. However, the `result.data` property might also contain an error message or be `null`/`undefined` in case of a service error, which would then be sent with a 200 status code. This can lead to clients receiving successful status codes for operations that actually failed, making error detection difficult. For example, if a service function returns `{ data: null, error: 'Agent not found', status: 404 }`, the current logic correctly sends a 404. But if it returns `{ data: { error: 'Agent not found' }, status: 200 }`, it would be treated as a success. The `result.error` property should be the primary and sole indicator of an error, and `result.data` should not contain error informatio

   322→function sendServiceResult(res: ServerResponse, result: any) {  
   323→  // Presence of result.error is the sole indicator of an error response;  
   324→  // result.data may also be present (e.g. partial results) but must not  
   325→  // suppress error reporting.  
   326→  if (result.error) {  
   327→    sendJson(res, result.status || 500, { error: result.error }, result.headers)

   330→  }  
   331→}

   333→function getHeader(req: IncomingMessage, name: string): string | null {  
   334→  const val = req.headers[name.toLowerCase()]  
   335→  return typeof val === 'string' ? val : null  
   336→}

   338→function getQuery(url: string): Record<string, string> {

   342→    if (typeof v === 'string') q[k] = v  
   343→  }  
   344→  return q

    20→### BUG: Race condition in `handleBuild` due to `clearPoll` placement  
    21→**Severity**: high  
    22→**Location**: `handleBuild`  
    23→**Problem**: The `clearPoll()` call at the beginning of `handleBuild` is intended to prevent leaks from rapid re-clicks. However, if a user clicks "Quick Build" multiple times very quickly, it's possible for `clearPoll()` to clear a `pollRef.current` that was just set by a *previous* invocation of `handleBuild` that is still in the process of setting up its own poll. This could lead to a poll not being started for the most recent build request, or an existing poll being prematurely cleared before it has a chance to complete.  
    24→**Fix**: The `clearPoll()` should be called *after* the initial `fetch` request for a new build has successfully started and returned a `buildId`, and *before* a new `setInterval` is potentially set. Thi

## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-03-22 20:01:16]*

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #FF9800; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

Now I have the complete file. Let me analyze all four bugs and apply the fixes.  

**Bug 1 (high):** Race condition — `clearPoll()` at top of `handleBuild` should move to after the successful fetch response, before setting up a new poll interval.  

**Bug 2 (medium):** Inconsistent error handling — initial fetch error path calls `res.json()` without a try/catch, which can throw if the response body isn't valid JSON.  

**Bug 3 (low):** `setTimeout` in `copyInstallCommand` not cleared on unmount — need a `copyTimeoutRef`.  

**Bug 4 (low):** `disabled` prop check order in "Push to GitHub" button — `!isComplete || disabled` should be `disabled || !isComplete`.  

Now applying all fixes:  

</div>

## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-03-22 20:01:26]*

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #FF9800; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

Now I have the complete picture. The `ServiceResult<T>` type is:  
```typescript
export interface ServiceResult<T> {
  data?: T
  error?: string   // always a string when present
  status: number   // ALWAYS defined (required field)
}
```

This is the key insight: `status` is a **required** field on `ServiceResult`, not optional. And `error` is typed as `string | undefined`. So:  

**Bug 1** (medium): Inconsistent error response structure — `result.error` is always `string` when present (per the type), so the inconsistency worry is actually a non-issue from the type perspective. However, in the route the error is returned as `{ error: result.error }` which is consistent with all other error responses. This is NOT a real bug.  

**Bug 2** (low): `result.status` potentially `undefined` — but `status` is a **required** (non-optional) field on `ServiceResult`. However, TypeScript's type system doesn't prevent a runtime undefined if the service ever returns an object without status. Looking at the service code, all error returns explicitly set `status`. But the real root issue here is: looking at the route code on line 34, `{ status: result.status }` — if `result.status` were ever undefined (which the type says it can't be, but as a defensive measure), NextResponse.json would use a wrong status. The fix is to add `|| 500` as a fallback.  

Wait — let me re-read the type: `status: number` — this is NOT optional (no `?`). So TypeScript guarantees it's always defined. However, the findings report says to add `|| 500` as a fallback. Let me check if there's a TypeScript strict mode issue or if the type was recently changed.  

</div>

## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-03-22 20:02:10]*

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #FF9800; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

Now I have the complete picture. Let me analyze all bugs precisely:  

**Bug 1 (medium) - Inconsistent Error Response Structure:**  
The route at line 34 returns `{ error: result.error }` which is consistent with all other error paths. However, `result.error` is typed as `string | undefined` (optional field in `ServiceResult`). When `result.error` is truthy (line 31 check), it is a string. The type is consistent. The concern about inconsistency is about the `result.error` value potentially being non-string at runtime — but the `ServiceResult<T>` type defines `error?: string`, so all service functions always return string errors. This is NOT actually a bug in the route — it's a valid concern but the type system enforces `error` is always a string.  

**Bug 2 (low) - Potential undefined status from `scanRepo`:**  
Looking at `ServiceResult<T>`: `status: number` — it is required, NOT optional. So TypeScript guarantees it is always set. All service error returns explicitly set `status`. However, comparing to sibling routes (`build/route.ts` line 21, `push/route.ts` line 89), they all use `{ status: result.status }` without a fallback — the established pattern. So adding `|| 500` here would create an inconsistency with the pattern of all other routes in this codebase.  

But wait — the `build/route.ts` success case at line 24 passes `{ status: result.status }` for the success path too, while `scan-repo/route.ts` line 37 returns `NextResponse.json(result.data)` WITHOUT passing the status for the success case. Looking at `push/route.ts` line 92 — same pattern, no status on success. So scan-repo matches push for success path. Both build's success uses `result.status` explicitly while push and scan-repo don't. This is a minor inconsistency but not the bug flagged.  

The two real bugs found are:  
1. **Bug 2 is the real bug**: `result.status` could be `undefined` in a defensive runtime sense — the TypeScript type requires `number` but the fix suggested (`|| 500`) guards against potential future breakage or any service that incorrectly omits `status`. This is a legitimate defensive fix.  
2. **Bug 1**: The `result.error` inconsistency — since the type is `string`, this is not truly a bug in practice, but the concern about type safety is valid.  

Looking at the actual code more carefully: The route code on line 31-36 is:  
```typescript
if (result.error) {
  return NextResponse.json(
    { error: result.error },
    { status: result.status }
  )
}
```

The `ServiceResult.status` is `number` (required). `ServiceResult.error` is `string | undefined`. Both bugs have the same fix: add `|| 500` to the status. This is the only real structural fix needed.  

Now let me look at Bug 1 more carefully. The report says there's inconsistency between the `{ error: string }` pattern used elsewhere and the `result.error` directly. Looking at the route, all paths already return `{ error: <some string> }` — the early validation errors all return `{ error: 'string literal' }`, and the service res  

... [347 more chars truncated]

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #FF9800; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

Now I'll apply the fix. The root cause of Bug 2 is that `result.status` is passed directly to `NextResponse.json` without a fallback. While the `ServiceResult` type requires `status: number`, a defensive `|| 500` guards against any future service implementation that might omit it (same fix both findings point to). This also resolves the related Bug 1 concern by ensuring `result.error` (which is `string` per the type) is always passed as-is — the error structure is already consistent.  

The only code change needed is adding `|| 500` as a fallback status on the `scanRepo` error path:

## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-03-22 20:02:20]*

<details>
<summary>🔧 Tool: Edit -- `route.ts`</summary>

**Input:**

**File:** `/Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/.claude/worktrees/rck-9a4b2a/app/api/plugin-builder/scan-repo/route.ts`

```
    if (result.error) {
      return NextResponse.json(
        { error: result.error },
        { status: result.status }
      )
    }
```

**New:**  
```
    if (result.error) {
      return NextResponse.json(
        { error: result.error },
        // Fall back to 500 if the service omits a status code, preventing an accidental 200 OK on error
        { status: result.status ?? 500 }
      )
    }
```

    10→  
    11→export async function POST(request: NextRequest) {  
    12→  try {  
    13→    const body = await request.json()  
    14→  
    15→    if (!body.url || typeof body.url !== 'string') {

## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-03-22 20:08:02]*

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #FF9800; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

Now I have a complete picture. Let me analyze each bug from the findings:  

**Bug 1 (activeOps double-decrement):** The `buildDispatched` flag is already correctly in place. When `buildDispatched = true`, the `catch` block does NOT decrement `activeOps` (guarded by `if (!buildDispatched)`), and `runBuild`'s `finally` block handles the decrement exactly once. When `buildDispatched = false` (error before dispatch), only the `catch` block decrements. The reviewer's analysis was a false positive — the fix is already correct. No change needed.  

**Bug 2 (fs.rm silent failure in eviction):** The reviewer self-corrects and says "No code change is strictly necessary." This is a design note, not a correctness bug. No change needed.  

**Bug 3 (MAX_BUILD_RESULTS eviction logic):** The reviewer self-corrects: "The logic for determining `toRemove` is correct in terms of quantity." Performance/design note only. No change needed.  

**Bug 4 (path traversal / logical inversion):** The reviewer explicitly self-corrects: "My analysis of the problem was flawed. The current validation is actually correct and robust." The code at line 168 uses `!SAFE_PATH_SEGMENT_RE.test(skill.marketplace)` which correctly means "if it does NOT match the safe pattern, return error." No change needed.  

**Bug 5 (execPromise maxBuffer):** Performance/configuration note. The reviewer says "increase maxBuffer." Let me check the current value.

   713→      if (entry.isFile() && !entry.isSymbolicLink() && entry.name.endsWith('.sh')) {  
   714→        scripts.push({  
   715→          name: entry.name,  
   716→          path: `scripts/${entry.name}`,  
   717→        })  
   718→      }  
   719→    }  
   720→  } catch {  
   721→    // No scripts directory  
   722→  }  
   723→  
   724→  return scripts  
   725→}  
   726→  
   727→/**

   731→  return url  
   732→    .replace(/^https?:\/\//, '')

   740→/**  
   741→ * Promisified execFile with stdout capture.  
   742→ */  
   743→function execPromise(  
   744→  command: string,  
   745→  args: string[],  
   746→  options: { cwd?: string; timeout?: number } = {}  
   747→): Promise<string> {  
   748→  return new Promise((resolve, reject) => {  
   749→    execFile(command, args, {  
   750→      cwd: options.cwd,  
   751→      timeout: options.timeout || 60000,  
   752→      maxBuffer: 2 * 1024 * 1024, // 2MB (reduced from 10MB)  
   753→    }, (error, stdout, stderr) => {  
   754→      if (error) {  
   755→        const err = error as any  
   756→        err.stderr = stderr  
   757→        reject(err)  
   758→      } else {  
   759→        resolve(stdout)  
   760→      }  
   761→    })  
   762→  })  
   763→}

## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-03-22 20:08:22]*

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #FF9800; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

Now I have a clear picture. The comment says "2MB (reduced from 10MB)" — this is suspicious. The reviewer flags this as a bug because the buffer was reduced from 10MB to 2MB. Git clone outputs for large repos, and build script outputs, can easily exceed 2MB. The comment itself acknowledges the reduction. This is a genuine correctness issue: git operations can fail with `ENOBUFS` when output exceeds 2MB, causing builds to fail even when the underlying command succeeds.  

Let me look at the remaining bugs (Bug 6: symlinks — self-corrected, Bug 7: sanitizeSourceName — self-corrected, Bug 8: runBuild cleanup) and verify Bug 8 more carefully.  

The `runBuild` function does NOT remove `buildDir` after a successful or failed build. The `evictStaleBuildResults` function is the only cleanup mechanism, which runs before new builds start. This means build directories accumulate until the next eviction. However, the findings say `scanRepo` and `pushToGitHub` do clean up immediately. This inconsistency means build artifacts can linger. But the report marks this as **low** severity and the suggested fix is to add `fs.rm` at the end of the `try` block — however, this would break `getBuildStatus` because clients poll for output files in `buildDir` via `outputPath`. The note says this is a design concern.  

After careful analysis, the only genuine correctness fix the report identifies is the `maxBuffer` being too small (the comment confirms it was deliberately reduced from 10MB to 2MB, which is a regression). All other bugs were self-corrected by the reviewer or are design notes.  

Let me fix the `maxBuffer` issue by restoring it to 10MB, which the comment itself acknowledges was the prior value:  

</div>
